All relationships, regardless of gender, regardless of whether friendships or partners, are investments to me - and the type of investment in which the payoff is non-material.

#Love
#Relationship
#Curiosity
#Research

So I had a relationship but then I was 24 and he was 21. In a way, it's easy to end a relationship but I realize and do a lot of research that a relationship is behavior and comes from the most subconscious and primal needs. Even though we call it modern human we still have that paleolithic emotions that drive us to make decision making.

So I got the idea that I wanna be with him even though he kinda pulling away, but I wanna study his behavior or even be there even though he may have someone else. But I bet this problem is going to be repeated again and again.

So kinda make this relationship become my experimental and study case. If I can understand these issues then I learn something that I can apply in the future.

#adviceüó£Ô∏è

Growing up, I often heard the older generation talk about the 5Cs as the true measure of success‚ÄîCash, Car, Condo, Credit Card, and Country Club Membership. Attaining all 5 was considered living the Singaporean dream. I used to think this idea was outdated, but a recent experience made me question if it still holds weight today.

I went on a date with a girl I met at a friend‚Äôs party. We had been texting for a few weeks and decided to meet. Turns out, she had done her ‚Äúresearch‚Äù on me beforehand‚Äîshe found my LinkedIn, socials, and even mentioned knowing my industry is lucrative.

The date took an uncomfortable turn when she began probing into my finances, asking how much I spend and why I don‚Äôt own a car despite earning above average. (For context, I work in investment banking, draw a five-figure salary, but live modestly‚Äîspending about $1K monthly while saving, investing, and paying off my mortgage.)

Of course, I didn‚Äôt want to share too much on a first date, so I explained that owning a car wasn‚Äôt practical since my apartment in the CBD is just a 5-7 minute walk to work. She responded by saying other guys with CBD apartments also own cars and that I should ‚Äúaim higher.‚Äù She even joked that I shouldn‚Äôt make excuses for not affording one.

Though I stayed calm and didn‚Äôt let her comments affect me, it left me wondering: Are Singaporeans still chasing the 5Cs? Should we still be judged by material possessions, or is it time to redefine success beyond these outdated ideals?
